text:
My original plan was for an egg salad recipe I had chosen that was a little fussier than this.  However, after an earlier experience today with a recipe with a more "complicated flavor," I decided to play it safe and go on the basic side with this recipe instead.  It IS delicious, taking me back to earlier days and a simpler style of cooking. (For me that would mean waaaay back in the day :)  I mean, didn't everyone's mom make egg salad just like this?  This is good just as is, but you can doll it up any way you like.  For me, that meant adding celery, because for us it just isn't egg salad without it.  But in the end, this is an egg salad recipe for what it is -  a good, basic, classic, egg salad, and not for all the fussier things it isn't.

text:
Perfect...... after some tweaking.  I hate when people drastically change recipes, but I couldnt find anything on here with all the KEY ingredients for great egg salad.  This recipe had a great start.  I just added some finely diced celery for crunch, 1 tsp dill weed (gotta have dill in your egg salad sandwich), 1/2 tsp onion powder instead of the green onions (didnt have any on hand) and used dijon mustard for a little more flavor.  Turned out great, I ate half of it before it even made it to the fridge for lunch the next day.

text:
Good basic recipe (which is what I was looking for).  I left out the onion on personal preference.  I added a tiny bit of pickle juice to give it some oomph, next time I think I'll add more.

To heck with dicing the eggs by hand (it takes FOREVER), I used my Pampered Chef chopper.  Took just minutes to chop up all the eggs!

For perfect hard-cooked eggs, the Broiler & Egg Association of Minnesota says to place eggs in single layer in covered saucepan in cold water, bring to boil, remove from heat and let stand for 15 minutes.  Once the time has elapsed, place eggs in ice water until cool.  This works beautifully - the eggs are done to perfection, there's no green edges, and they peeled quite easily, no tearing!

text:
Great basic recipe. A tip: peel the eggs immediately (the shells come off more easily then).  I added curry powder (always a "must-have ingredient" for egg salad in our house), and I went lighter on the scallions. I also added a bit of tumeric, which heightens the yellow color and adds a valuable nutrient. (Tumeric is an antioxidant, an anti-inflammatory, and an anti-carcinogenic).

text:
Yum! Deliciously satisfying! I didn't have green onions, so onion powder served as the pinch hitter today. I also added an eyeballed amount of Old Bay (although sometimes I use Lawry's). I used my standard method for boiling my eggs 14 minutes and giving them a 10 minute ice bath afterward before peeling them under cold, running water. I served this egg salad on honey-wheat bread with a slice of swiss cheese and a generous handful of spring greens on each sandwich. A serving of sweet potato fries and iced tea rounded out this lovely Mother's Day lunch, and was a hit with my hubby and 3 year-old daughter!  This is definitely a nice recipe on its own, but is certainly open to variation depending on what you have on hand, or your mood! Thanks for the submission, wifeyluvs2cook!

text:
This is a quick way to make a filling lunch for days that seem to go faster than they should. It's no trouble to make in the morning, and ensures that you have something great to look forward to at lunchtime. I made this with low-fat mayonnaise, stone-ground mustard, and leeks since they were what I had at hand. Although my sandwich fell apart because the egg salad was a little runny, it still was very delicious. I'd use less mayo next time, and probably make it the night before and chill it so it holds together better. Thanks for the recipe!

text:
The only things I added/changed was: I used finely diced sweet onions instead of green onion (didn't have any), I diced up a celery rib to throw in there for that crunch that I love, and I also added 1 tsp of dill weed. I made it while the eggs were still very warm, and that made it very thick and creamy. It made enough to last us almost 3 days total, and it didn't get runny in the fridge at all. Actually, somehow, it got better and better as the days passed. Thank you....it is definitely a keeper!

text:
The concern I have is, the instructions on how to boil the eggs.  I used these directions several times and it would take me an hour to peel the shells off the eggs.  The issue is the putting the eggs into the water and bring to a boil.  It's left up to interpretation WHEN the water is "boiling".  Leaving the eggs in for 10-12 min. to too vague.  My daughter came home for a visit and actually showed me a easy...fail proof way to hard boil an egg. 
   Saras hard boiled eggs:
	Fill colander about  full
	Add salt
	Set to high, bring water to a rapid boil
	Reduce to medium, to a steady boil and wait 2 min.
	Carefully add a dozen eggs
	Partially cover colander with the lid and wait 15 min.
	Remove colander and eggs from heat and let sit for 2 min.
	Add eggs to a bowl and immediately put into fridge
	Let stand in fridge for at least 1 hour before shelling
	Tap the large end of the eggs and a couple of times on the side
	Egg shells are super easy to peel
	Grate eggs and add onions, celery, mayonnaise and season as you like.

Trust me...this method works much better than what is posted on google.

text:
Egg salad is a tricky thing, because so many people have different variations on what they like in it. That being said, I think this is a perfect base recipe to jump from for any starter cook. I usually just threw the basic mayo/mustard/spices in to taste without measurement and it came out differently each time. This gives me good consistency in acquiring my start mixture every time. I like the paprika.

Since I have basically used this as only a base, and it is decent on its own, I have made alterations to spice it up better to my tastes. Green pepper is not always available in my house, but dill pickles almost certainly are, so a 1/4 cup of chopped pickles gives the salad a good boost and a little crunch. I add a few shakes of celery seed when I don't have celery to add for flavor. Also a little finely chopped onion is a good addition at times as well.

This is a wonderful recipe.  Any changes made are due to personal preferences.
We like gherkins so we add one to two tablespoons of chopped gherkins and reduced the green onions  to one-fourth cup and switched the yellow mustard to one-half teaspoon dry mustard.
To those who add red or green peppers, due to their water content, egg salad will be runny the next day.

This recipe for egg salad is great! I have always winged it when it came to measurements.. but this was a good guide. country:

text:
I've made my egg salad with these ingredients for about 60 years, however, I use less mayonnaise and more mustard.  3-4 years ago, I was at my daughter's home, and teaching my 9 year old grandson how to make it.  The good news is that we had all the ingredients, the bad news is, there wasn't enough regular mustard.  So, we improvised!  My daughter is a mustard aficionado!  So, Alex & I picked Grey Poupon Dijon mustard, added 2/3rds French's mustard (all we had!) and 1/3rd Dijon mustard.  It was a *hit*!!!  We prepared the eggs the same, except for chopping them.  I've found that using a large grater works better for my family, but if you prefer a finer chop than pictured, try using the egg slicer once, then chop against the slices (after transferring slices intact to your less dominant hand) and gently chop quarter inch chunks.  Later, Michelle's family wanted it spicy, so I now add a small amount of cayenne (shades of Chef John!) or horseradish.  Taste for salt, pepper and spice & try on any kind of bread.  I prefer sourdough French, but for friends I often use freshly made croissants.  HTH! Blessings!!!

I'd never thought to add mustard, and it was a good addition.  
When my eggs are done cooking I dump the hot water and crack the shell of each egg as I add it to cold water - then I shell them under running cold water, laying them on a towel and wiping dry before using the pastry blender to chop them in a bowl - makes the job so much easier!  Also, use cooking onion instead of green onions.  I do prefer the stronger taste.  At 72 yrs old it's still nice to learn new ways of doing things.

userID:
12969973
Display Name:
Frank Truth
isPro:
False
followersCount:
0
followingCount:
0
madeRecipesCount:
1
favoritesCount:

recipesCount:
0
reviewsCount:

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5674169.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Add 1/2 cup of water to a rice cooker. Measure water from bottom of meniscus. Add a dash of vinegar. Prick seven eggs. Place 7 eggs in the steaming basket of a rice cooker. When the cooker dings, the eggs are finished. You have perfect hard-boiled eggs in roughly 12 minutes. Place eggs in bowel and run water on eggs for one or two minutes. Then place eggs in ice water for ten minutes. Roll eggs on table till it is covered with cracks. Start cracking shell at the to top of the egg, the wide part. Then carefully break shell away under running water. Use an egg slicer to slice the hard boiled eggs first in one direction, then in another. To the above recipe add a little less mayonnaise. Use Spectrum Canola mayonnaise purchased from Whole Foods Grocery store. Add half a sweet onion finely chopped. Use fancy paprika. Double the quantity of paprika. Use fresh coarsely ground Tellicherry peppercorns. Add one clove of minced garlic. Add Dijon mustard and Honey Cup honey mustard. Add half a cap (not half a cup) of lemon juice, and a little red wine vinegar. Add dried or fresh dill weed and celery seed. Add a little garlic powder and onion power. Add a dash of Mrs. Dash. Optional: add chopped celery and/or a tiny amount of chopped pickle and/or a tiny amount of pickle relish. Or add a little curry powder in place of pickle or pickle relish. Or add chipotle powder. Start with a little bit of each added ingredient, then add a little more to taste. Don't overpower with spices.

text:
Excellent egg salad recipe!  Thanks!  Easy peel eggs...boil the water, pierce the rounded part of the egg with an egg piercer, lower the eggs into the boiling water with a slotted spoon.  Cover and boil for 12 min. Drain - shake the pan to crack the shells.  Run very cold water on the eggs and start peeling.  Sometimes an egg will 'peel' itself when you have shaken the pan!

text:
Perfect egg salad, basic but simply delicious and it's a classic. I don't like a lot of flavors going on with egg salad, and this fits the bill. I make my egg salad like this all the time, but unfortunately I didn't have any green onions, so I had to do without. This still turned out great. If you don't have any green onions, a dash of onion powder would work also. I used herbed wraps and some iceberg lettuce and this was a wonderful lunch. Honestly, my favorite way to have egg salad is between 2 slices of toasted white bread, but the wraps was a nice change. Simplicity at it's best! :)

text:
Very nice recipe.  Works great for sandwiches.  Like other reviewers had said, you can add just about anything to this recipe to make your own.  

For all the Instant Pot owners,  add water to the IP, place trivet on the bottom of the pan.  Place eggs on trivet.  Place lid on pot and make sure it's on sealing position.  5 minutes under pressure and 5 minutes natural release.  Remove eggs and put in ice water.  Best eggs ever....easy to peel and perfect every time.

I agree with the other reviews on here, this is a really great egg salad base to which you can add your own twist to it. I added dill and thinly sliced celery to my egg salad. I didn't have any yellow mustard, but I had left over sweet hot mustard from Hickory Farms. I think it tasted even better with that. 

In terms of cooking the eggs, I followed a tip another reviewer left on here, and the eggs came out beautiful and vibrant yellow in the center. The key was to cook it in boiling water 5 minutes,  take it off the heat, and then let it sit for an additional 10 minutes. Definitely adding this to the recipe book.

As others have said I loved this as a base recipe. 
These are the changes/additions I made:
Use 1/3 cup mayo (vs. 1/2)
Use 1 Tablespoon Grey Poupon Mustard (vs. 1 tsp yellow)
Use 1/3 cup chopped Vidalia onion
Add 2 dash's Franks hot sauce and a dusting of cayenne pepper, 
Add dried (or fresh) parsley; 
Next time I'll add celery too.  :)

text:
I prefer a baseline for salt with the addition or to taste, but anyway a very good basic recipe. I did note that people have trouble peeling the eggs. I have a method that has yet to fail me. Steam the eggs. Bring water to boil on med-high then add the eggs. For 8 eggs, steam them 15 minutes. Then put them in ice water immediately and let them cool about 15-20 minutes. I have never had trouble peeling the eggs using this method. For 6 eggs I steam them 12 minutes.

text:
This is a good basic recipe. But, because I was quadrupling the recipe and making it the day before for a crowd, and because I like some crunch and zip to my egg salad, I made these changes:  I used onion powder so the onions wouldn't weep, added some chopped celery (dried well on paper towels) and some pickle relish well-drained and blotted on paper towels.  The salad stayed a nice thick texture that way. I also added a light shake of cayenne pepper to the mix!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This is a very good basic recipe as is and as noted in recipe I used less green onion and rated it at this point as 5 stars. But I  needed some punch so added sweet and dill relish along with 1 small rib of finely minced celery and ate it open-faced on toasted mild rye bread - VERY GOOD.   Probably depending on  eggs (they are sold by weight not necessarily by size or count) they should boil for 2-3 minutes to avoid not being fully cooked then covered and removed from heat to rest for about 15 min.  Have a container of iced water ready and immediately plunge eggs in for about 5 minutes.  Crack initially on the small end of the egg (where the air gathers) then crack entire shell all about gently and peel under small stream of running cold water (be sure to get peeling started under that layer of film that can sometimes be present).  I had struggled for years blaming the eggs for ragged peeling but since I've been using this method I rarely ever have that trouble - they are beautiful every time!  With this method I can't recommend waiting to peel them after they have been refrigerated for a time since I haven't tried it. I hope this is helpful .  Thank you for submitting the recipe.

Been making a similar recipe for years but add in fine diced celery, bell pepper, dill pickle, and other fruits and vegetables.   (Yes, peppers and pickles are fruits.) It turned out perfect considering i only was able to use 6 eggs put i cut down a little on mayonnaise and mustard. As for paprika i used the full amount it asked for, and i used salt and pepper. Pepper i used the perfect amount i always like when people say how much they used for salt and pepper so i get a better idea, but unfortunately I didn't measure the amount i used this time. All in all i added to much salt in the end sadly but i know my husband can complain i do not put enough sometimes so we will see how he looks it.

text:
I LOVED this recipe!!  I have made it exactly as is before, and it was wonderful. :) 

This time, however, I did make a few minor changes.  I actually tripled this recipe (birthday party!), and I  wanted to play around a bit.  My tripled recipe called for 1-1/2 cups mayonnaise; I used 1 cup mayonnaise and 1/2 cup plain non-fat yogurt.  I did not have green onions, but I did have a package of chives, so I chopped them up in place of the green onions. 

Also - I have learned that the secret to the best egg salad possible is CELERY SEED.  I added about 1 tbsp or so to my tripled recipe, and I let the finished egg salad set in the fridge for a couple of hours so that the flavors could meld well.  

YUMMY!!!

text:
I'm on the have-to-use-up-Easter-eggs bandwagon.  This is a wonderful base recipe as it is.  Because it's such a great base, you can do almost anything with it.  Like some crunch?  Add some chopped celery.  Like a little more tang?  Add some extra mustard, some relish, or some pickle juice.  Want more color?  Add some red bell peppers and/or the aforementioned celery.  A little more heat, maybe?  Pinch of cayenne will do just the trick.  Like dill in your egg salad?  Add some if you want it!  I like recipes like this that taste wonderful as is, but have enough versatility to let you do whatever you like with it and still end up with a great result.

text:
I didn't have any green onion in the house, so I used yellow onion instead. Also, Dijon mustard tastes much better in egg salad than yellow mustard, in my opinion. I made a bunch of different samples of egg salad (having no choice, but to alter this recipe a bit with the lack of green onion). I used different ingredients in each sample. So far, my favorite combination is Mayo (I used "Just Mayo"), dijon mustard (Grey Poupon) and paprika. Although, I also really like the combination of mayo (again, I used "Just Mayo"), dijon mustard, yellow onion and dill weed. I would not recommend using curry. I tried it and didn't like it at all.

He told me he liked egg salad and after I made him one, he scoffed it down and promptly asked for another. It lasts 2 or 3 days at the latest in the fridge in an airtight container.

text:
Made this the other day and I have to admit that it needed a few adjustments.  First, the egg boiling method threw me for a bit of a loop but I tried it anyway.  Eggs came out okay but the yoke was much darker yellow than I had expected.  They seemed firm enough but maybe I needed to let them cook a bit longer.  Ended up letting the whole thing sit for a day and it did fine, but when tasted the whole thing seemed rather bland.  Ended up adding some salt (which improved the taste even though I added a little too much) and still needed something.  Remembered that my mom used to put relish in her egg salad and that was what I was missing.  Didn't have any on hand so made due with chopping up some dill pickle slices and it was better.  Going to make it again (with proper ingredients on hand) and will probably let the eggs boil for a couple of minutes before taking them off the stove.

This is a great recipe for the ratio; however, I like less mayo - so add only 1 Tablespoon of mayonnaise AND 1/4 cup sour cream or 1/4 cup of plain Greek yogurt. 1/4 cup of Yellow Mustard. Add a scant teaspoon of Vinegar. Add a dash of Celery Salt. If it is too "liquidic", then use 10 hard boiled eggs instead of 8. (f you do not like green onions, then substitute celeryOR chopped dill pickles)

text:
I'd give this three and a half if possible - it's an awesome Base - but not really great as is.  It's just bland as written.  The second time I made it I went made it about 1/4mustard and 3/4mayonnaise - and replaced the green onion with relish.  This was a great improvement - but next time I'm going to make it half mustard and half mayonnaise for the base.  (in other words 1/4 cup of each).  I'll also probably double the paprika - or add a 1/4 tsp of chili powder or cayenne - something to give just a tiny kick.  I'll let you know how that comes out. It was definitely better with more mustard and the relish the second time around. This is a great base - but be ready to experiment (though that's half the fun or a recipe to me)

Chris and I made this one night during the week, (Actually I made this and Chris supervised!) and it came out awesome!!! It was super tasty!!! I took the leftovers to work the next day and it was just as good as the night before.   As for the directions on how to boil the eggs, the way the author of this recipe instructed did not work. The eggs we only partially cooked. We suggest keeping it on the burner for 15-20 minutes. It allows for easy peeling and a well cooked egg.   As many of the other cooks that reviewed this delicious recipe suggested, we too added small chunks of dill pickle.   We will most certainly will keep this easy and mouthwatering recipe handy!!!

text:
This was just so-so for me. I've never been a huge fan of egg salad, but I will eat it on occasion, hence my desire to try Wifey's recipe. The taste of this was decent, but it didn't WOW me. I love my mom's deviled eggs (a passed down recipe from my Grandma), so I tried to incorporate a few elements of her recipe with Wifey's. Although my attempt did not turn out as expected, it didn't "ruin" the outcome either. My only change (again, to mimic my mom's recipe) was to add another t of (plain) mustard and 4 t distilled white vinegar. Oh, and I added one small rib of celery, mainly because I wanted to use it up. I've been eating this on wheat bread with a slice of Boston lettuce for lunch so far this week. It is certainly simple and satisfying but, I don't think it will be a repeat with me. I guess I don't like egg salad that much after all. Thanks for sharing :)

text:
I rarely follow recipes for egg salad--I generally just add whatever and taste until I'm satisfied.  So I used this recipe as more of a jumping off point.  I used about 10 eggs instead of 8, but I used about the same amount of mayo.  I used a lot more mustard, but I love the flavor, and I also love paprika so added more of that as well.  I used pickles and cucumber for crunch and didn't have green onions.  I also tossed in a bit of parsley.  I served as finger sandwiches at a volunteer appreciation event at work, and they were completely finished before the event.  Other sandwiches were served as well, but the egg salad was by far the most popular.  Thanks for the recipe!
